625\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cape_Verde" title="Economy of Cape Verde">Economy of Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="863" data-file-width="1106" decoding="async" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Cape_Verde.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Cape Verde\'s export products</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TACV_B757_D4-CBG_MUC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/TACV_B757_D4-CBG_MUC.jpg/250px-TACV_B757_D4-CBG_MUC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/TACV_B757_D4-CBG_MUC.jpg/375px-TACV_B757_D4-CBG_MUC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/TACV_B757_D4-CBG_MUC.jpg/500px-TACV_B757_D4-CBG_MUC.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TACV_B757_D4-CBG_MUC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cape Verdean national flag carrier TACV</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2834" data-file-width="4212" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg/250px-Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg/375px-Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg/500px-Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verde_Sal_pool.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A resort in <a href="/wiki/Sal,_Cape_Verde" title="Sal, Cape Verde">Sal</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cape Verde\'s notable economic growth and improvement in living conditions despite a lack of natural resources has garnered <a href="#International_recognition">international recognition</a>, with other countries and international organizations often providing <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development aid</a>. Since 2007, the UN has classified it as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_nation" title="Developing nation">developing nation</a> rather than a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" title="Least developed country">least developed country</a>.\n</p><p>Cape Verde has few <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>. Only five of the ten main islands (Santiago, Santo Ant&#227;o, S&#227;o Nicolau, Fogo, and Brava) normally support significant agricultural production,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and over 90% of all food consumed in Cape Verde is imported. Mineral resources include salt, <a href="/wiki/Pozzolana" title="Pozzolana">pozzolana</a> (a volcanic rock used in cement production), and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-17"><a href="#cite_note-bn-14">[14]</a></sup> Its small number of wineries making Portuguese-style wines have traditionally focused on the domestic market, but have recently met with some international acclaim. A number of wine tours of Cape Verde\'s various microclimates began to be offered in spring 2010 and can be arranged through the tourism office.\n</p><p>The economy of Cape Verde is service-oriented, with commerce, transport, and public services accounting for more than 70% of GDP.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although nearly 35% of the population lives in rural areas, agriculture and fishing contribute only about 9% of GDP. Light manufacturing accounts for most of the remainder. Fish and shellfish are plentiful, and small quantities are exported. Cape Verde has cold storage and freezing facilities and <a href="/wiki/Fish_processing" title="Fish processing">fish processing</a> plants in Mindelo, Praia, and on Sal. Expatriate Cape Verdeans contribute an amount estimated at about 20% of GDP to the domestic economy through <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-18"><a href="#cite_note-bn-14">[14]</a></sup>\nIn spite of having few natural resources and being semi-desert, the country boasts the highest living standards in the region, and has attracted thousands of immigrants of different nationalities.\n</p><p>Since 1991, the government has pursued market-oriented economic policies, including an open welcome to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_investors" title="Foreign investors">foreign investors</a> and a far-reaching <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a> programme. It established as top development priorities the promotion of a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> and of the private sector; the development of <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Cape_Verde" title="Tourism in Cape Verde">tourism</a>, light manufacturing industries, and fisheries; and the development of <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cape_Verde" title="Transport in Cape Verde">transport</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communications_in_Cape_Verde" title="Communications in Cape Verde">communications</a>, and energy facilities. From 1994 to 2000 about $407 million in foreign investments were made or planned, of which 58% were in tourism,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> 17% in industry, 4% in infrastructure, and 21% in fisheries and services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-19"><a href="#cite_note-bn-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, on four islands a wind farm was built that supplies about 30% of the electricity of the country. It is one of the top countries for renewable energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 2000 and 2009, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_GDP" title="Real GDP">real GDP</a> increased on average by over 7 percent a year, well above the average for Sub-Saharan countries and faster than most small island economies in the region. Strong economic performance was bolstered by one of the fastest growing tourism industries in the world, as well as by substantial capital inflows that allowed Cape Verde to build up national currency reserves to the current 3.5 months of imports. Unemployment has been falling rapidly, and the country is on track to achieve most of the UN Millennium Development Goals &#8211; including halving its 1990 poverty level.\n</p><p>In 2007, Cape Verde joined the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO) and in 2008 the country graduated from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" title="Least developed country">Least Developed Country</a> (LDC) to Middle Income Country (MIC) status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cape Verde has significant cooperation with Portugal at every level of the economy, which has led it to link its currency first to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_escudo" title="Portuguese escudo">Portuguese escudo</a> and, in 1999, to the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>. On 23 June 2008 Cape Verde became the 153rd member of the WTO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CV-praia-in_der_avenida_cabral.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/CV-praia-in_der_avenida_cabral.jpg/220px-CV-praia-in_der_avenida_cabral.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/CV-praia-in_der_avenida_cabral.jpg/330px-CV-praia-in_der_avenida_cabral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/CV-praia-in_der_avenida_cabral.jpg/440px-CV-praia-in_der_avenida_cabral.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CV-praia-in_der_avenida_cabral.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cabral Avenue, one of the main symbols of Cape Verde\'s development.</div></div></div>\n<p>In early January 2018, the government announced that the minimum wage would be raised to 13,000 CVE (US$140 or EUR 130) per month, from 11,000 CVE, which was effective in mid-January 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The European Commission\'s total allocation for the period of 2008&#8211;2013 foreseen for Cape Verde to address "poverty reduction, in particular in rural and periurban areas where women are heading the households, as well as good governance" amounts to &#8364;54.1 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Cape_Verde" title="Tourism in Cape Verde">Tourism in Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mindelo_portogrande.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="262" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Mindelo_portogrande.jpg/220px-Mindelo_portogrande.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Mindelo_portogrande.jpg/330px-Mindelo_portogrande.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/Mindelo_portogrande.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mindelo_portogrande.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Yachts in Porto Grande, Mindelo on the island of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_Cape_Verde" title="S&#227;o Vicente, Cape Verde">S&#227;o Vicente</a>. Tourism is a growing source of income on the islands.</div></div></div>\n<p>Cape Verde\'s strategic location at the crossroads of mid-Atlantic air and sea lanes has been enhanced by significant improvements at <a href="/wiki/Mindelo" title="Mindelo">Mindelo</a>\'s harbour (<a href="/wiki/Porto_Grande_Bay" title="Porto Grande Bay">Porto Grande</a>) and at <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_International_Airport" title="Am&#237;lcar Cabral International Airport">Sal\'s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_International_Airport" title="Nelson Mandela International Airport">Praia\'s international airports</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Aristides_Pereira_International_Airport" title="Aristides Pereira International Airport">new international airport</a> was opened in Boa Vista in December 2007, and on the island of S&#227;o Vicente, the newest international airport (<a href="/wiki/Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_Airport" title="Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora Airport">Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora Airport</a>) in Cape Verde, was opened in late 2009. Ship repair facilities at Mindelo were opened in 1983.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-20"><a href="#cite_note-bn-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The major ports are Mindelo and Praia, but all other islands have smaller port facilities. In addition to the international airport on Sal, <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Cape_Verde" title="List of airports in Cape Verde">airports</a> have been built on all of the inhabited islands. All but the airports on Brava and <a href="/wiki/Santo_Ant%C3%A3o,_Cape_Verde" title="Santo Ant&#227;o, Cape Verde">Santo Ant&#227;o</a> enjoy scheduled air service. The archipelago has 3,050&#160;km (1,895&#160;mi) of roads, of which 1,010&#160;km (628&#160;mi) are paved, most using <a href="/wiki/Cobblestone" title="Cobblestone">cobblestone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-21"><a href="#cite_note-bn-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The country\'s future economic prospects depend heavily on the maintenance of aid flows, the encouragement of tourism, remittances, outsourcing labour to neighbouring African countries, and the momentum of the government\'s development programme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-22"><a href="#cite_note-bn-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdeans" title="Cape Verdeans">Cape Verdeans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cape_Verde" title="Demographics of Cape Verde">Demographics of Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape-Verde-demography.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="724" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cape-Verde-demography.png/220px-Cape-Verde-demography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cape-Verde-demography.png/330px-Cape-Verde-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Cape-Verde-demography.png/440px-Cape-Verde-demography.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cape-Verde-demography.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cape Verde\'s population, (1961&#8211;2003)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="902" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG/220px-Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG/330px-Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG/440px-Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Cap-Vert.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cape Verde\'s <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a>, 2005</div></div></div>\n<p>The official Census recorded that Cape Verde had a population of 512,096 in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> A large proportion (236,000) of Cape Verdeans live on the main island, Santiago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cvp_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-cvp-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Cape Verde archipelago was uninhabited when the Portuguese discovered it in 1456. The modern population of Cape Verde descends from the mixture of European settlers and African slaves who were brought to the islands to work on Portuguese plantations. Most Cape Verdeans are therefore <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">mulattos</a>, also called <a href="/wiki/Mesti%C3%A7o" title="Mesti&#231;o">mesti&#231;os</a> in Portuguese.  Another term is <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples#Portuguese_Africa" title="Creole peoples">creole</a>, meaning those of mixed native-born African and native-born European descent.\n</p><p>European input included <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> seamen who were granted land by the Portuguese Empire, followed by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> settlers and exiles, as well as Portuguese Muslims (ethnic <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>) and Portuguese Jews (ethnic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardim" title="Sephardim">Sephardim</a>), both of these religious groups were victims of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Inquisition" title="Portuguese Inquisition">Inquisition</a>. Other immigrants came from places such as the Netherlands, France, Britain, the Arab countries (especially Lebanon and Morocco), China (especially from Macau), India, Indonesia, South America, and North America (including people of Portuguese and African descent) and were absorbed into the mesti&#231;o population.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_Claridalia_(18).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2912" data-file-width="4368" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_Claridalia_%2818%29.jpg/220px-Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_Claridalia_%2818%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_Claridalia_%2818%29.jpg/330px-Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_Claridalia_%2818%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_Claridalia_%2818%29.jpg/440px-Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_Claridalia_%2818%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_Claridalia_(18).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People in <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">Santiago</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cape Verde\'s population in the 21st century is mostly <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples#Portuguese_Africa" title="Creole peoples">creole</a>; the capital city Praia accounts for a quarter of the country\'s population. Over 65% of the population in the archipelago live in urban centers, and the literacy rate is 89% (i.e., 93,3% among men aged 15 and above and 84,7% among women aged 15 and above) according to the 2017 National Statistics Bureau data.\nMany Cape Verdeans have since emigrated, mainly to the United States and Europe.\n</p><p>A genetic study revealed that the ancestry of the population in Cape Verde is predominantly European in the male line and West African in the female line; counted together the percentage is 56% African and 44% European.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The high degree of genetic and ethnic mixture of individuals is a result of centuries of migration.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Cape Verde\'s official language is Portuguese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-1">[1]</a></sup> It is the language of instruction and government. It is also used in newspapers, television, and radio.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">Cape Verdean Creole</a> is used colloquially and is the mother tongue of virtually all Cape Verdeans. The national constitution calls for the measures to give it parity with Portuguese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-1">[1]</a></sup> Cape Verdean Creole or Kriolu is a dialect continuum of a Portuguese-based <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole</a>. There is a substantial body of literature in Creole, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Creole" title="Santiago Creole">Santiago Creole</a> and the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente_Creole" title="S&#227;o Vicente Creole">S&#227;o Vicente Creole</a>. Creole has been gaining prestige since the nation\'s independence from Portugal.\n</p><p>The differences between the forms of the language within the islands have been a major obstacle in the way of standardization of the language. Some people have advocated the development of two standards: a North (Barlavento) standard, centered on the S&#227;o Vicente Creole, and a South (Sotavento) standard, centered on the Santiago Creole. <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Veiga_(writer)" title="Manuel Veiga (writer)">Manuel Veiga</a>, PhD, a linguist and Minister of Culture of Cape Verde, is the premier proponent of Kriolu\'s officialization and standardization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cape_Verde" title="Religion in Cape Verde">Religion in Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:DarkGrey"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 122.4374949739px; border-left-color:SkyBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:SkyBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:SkyBlue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 23.675858515503px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Religion in Cape Verde (2010)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pew_Forum&#160;&#8212;_Religion_in_Cape_Verde_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Forum_&#8212;_Religion_in_Cape_Verde-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> (78.7%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:SkyBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Christian (10.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkGrey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other or non-religious (10.9%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>Around 95% of the population are Christian. More than 85% of the population was nominally <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rf_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-rf-51">[51]</a></sup> For a minority of the population, Catholicism is <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretized</a> with African influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> denomination is the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Nazarene" title="Church of the Nazarene">Church of the Nazarene</a>; other groups include the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Assemblies_of_God" title="Assemblies of God">Assemblies of God</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Church_of_the_Kingdom_of_God" title="Universal Church of the Kingdom of God">Universal Church of the Kingdom of God</a>, and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">evangelical</a> groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rf_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-rf-51">[51]</a></sup> There is a small <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rf_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-rf-51">[51]</a></sup> There were <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Cape_Verde" title="History of the Jews in Cape Verde">Jewish</a> settlements on several islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atheists" title="Atheists">atheists</a> is estimated at less than 1% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rf_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-rf-51">[51]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration_and_immigration">Emigration and immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Emigration and immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_diaspora" title="Cape Verdean diaspora">Cape Verdean diaspora</a></div>\n<p>Today, more Cape Verdeans live abroad than in Cape Verde itself, with significant emigrant<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Cape Verdean communities in the United States (500,000 of Cape Verdean descent, with a major concentration on the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> coast from <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence, Rhode Island</a>, to <a href="/wiki/New_Bedford,_Massachusetts" title="New Bedford, Massachusetts">New Bedford, Massachusetts</a>).\n</p><p>There are significant Cape Verde populations in Portugal (150,000), <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> (45,000), <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="S&#227;o Tom&#233; and Pr&#237;ncipe">S&#227;o Tom&#233; and Pr&#237;ncipe</a> (25,000), <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> (25,000), the Netherlands (20,000, of which 15,000 are concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>), Spain (65,500), United Kingdom (35,500), France (25,000), Italy (10,000) <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> (7,000) and Scandinavia (7,000). There is a Cape Verdean community in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> numbering 8,000. A large number of Cape Verdeans and people of Cape Verdean descent who emigrated before 1975 are not included in these statistics, because Cape Verdeans had Portuguese passports before 1975.\n</p><p>The Chinese make up a sizable and important segment of the immigrant population in Cape Verde. The immigrants from the nearby West African coast make up the majority of foreigners in the country. Over the last several years, a few thousand Europeans and Latin Americans have settled in the country. On the islands, there are over 22,000 foreigners/naturalized Cape Verdeans who hail from over 90 countries around the world living and working on a permanent basis.\n</p><p>Over the years, Cape Verde has increasingly become a net immigration country due to its relative high per capita income, political and social stability, and freedom.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Emigrants from the Cape Verde islands to North America have a long history of involvement with the armed forces. Enlisting in aid of the Revolutionary War, the Civil War, the First and Second World Wars, as well as the Korean and Vietnam Wars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Cape Verdeans moved to places all over the world, from <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> to <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, and Argentina to northern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Cape_Verde" title="Health in Cape Verde">Health in Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PraiaCentrodeSa%C3%BAde.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="738" data-file-width="1445" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/PraiaCentrodeSa%C3%BAde.jpg/250px-PraiaCentrodeSa%C3%BAde.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/PraiaCentrodeSa%C3%BAde.jpg/375px-PraiaCentrodeSa%C3%BAde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/PraiaCentrodeSa%C3%BAde.jpg/500px-PraiaCentrodeSa%C3%BAde.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PraiaCentrodeSa%C3%BAde.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A health clinic in a residential area of Praia</div></div></div>\n<p>The infant mortality rate among Cape Verdean children between 0 and 5 years old is 15 per 1,000 live births according to the latest (2017) data from the National Statistics Bureau,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ine.cv_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ine.cv-57">[57]</a></sup> while the maternal mortality rate is 42 deaths per 100,000 live births. The HIV-AIDS prevalence rate among Cape Verdeans between 15 and 49 years old is 0.8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the latest data (2017) from the National Statistics Bureau,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ine.cv_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-ine.cv-57">[57]</a></sup> life expectancy at birth in Cape Verde is 76,2 years, that is, 72,2 years for males and 80,2 years for females. There are six hospitals in the Cape Verde archipelago: two central hospitals (one in the capital city of Praia and one in Mindelo, S&#227;o Vicente) and four regional hospitals (one in Santa Catarina (northern Santiago region), one on S&#227;o Ant&#227;o, one on Fogo, and one on Sal). In addition, there are 28 health centers, 35 sanitation centers and a variety of private clinics located throughout the archipelago.\n</p><p>Cape Verde\'s population is among the healthiest in Africa. Since its independence, it has greatly improved its health indicators. Besides having been promoted to the group of "medium development" countries in 2007, leaving the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries">least developed countries</a> category (which is only the second time it has happened to a country<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>), is currently the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index#Africa" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">10th best ranked</a> country in Africa in its <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.\n</p><p>The total expenditure for health was 7.1% of GDP (2015).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Cape_Verde" title="Education in Cape Verde">Education in Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Finalistas_do_jardim_infantil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="773" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Finalistas_do_jardim_infantil.jpg/250px-Finalistas_do_jardim_infantil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Finalistas_do_jardim_infantil.jpg/375px-Finalistas_do_jardim_infantil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Finalistas_do_jardim_infantil.jpg/500px-Finalistas_do_jardim_infantil.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Finalistas_do_jardim_infantil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A kindergarten graduation in Santiago island</div></div></div>\n<p>Although the Cape Verdean educational system is similar to the Portuguese system, over the years the local universities have been increasingly adopting the American educational system; for instance, all 10 existing universities in the country offer 4-year bachelor\'s degree programs as opposed to 5-year bachelor\'s degree programs that existed before 2010. Cape Verde has the second best educational system in Africa, after South Africa.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\nPrimary school education in Cape Verde is mandatory and free for children between the ages of 6 and 14 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, the net enrollment ratio for primary school was 85%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Approximately 90% of the total population over 15 years of age is literate, and roughly 25% of the population holds a college degree; a significant number of these college graduates hold doctorate degrees in different academic fields. Textbooks have been made available to 90 percent of school children, and 98 percent of the teachers have attended in-service teacher training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-60">[60]</a></sup> Although most children have access to education, some problems remain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_60-3"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-60">[60]</a></sup> For example, there is insufficient spending on school materials, lunches, and books.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_60-4"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  October&#160;2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 69 secondary schools throughout the archipelago (including 19 private secondary schools) and at least 10 universities in the country which are based on the two islands of Santiago and S&#227;o Vicente.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Universidade_de_Santiago.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Universidade_de_Santiago.jpg/220px-Universidade_de_Santiago.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Universidade_de_Santiago.jpg/330px-Universidade_de_Santiago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Universidade_de_Santiago.jpg/440px-Universidade_de_Santiago.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Universidade_de_Santiago.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University of Santiago</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2015, 23% of the Cape Verdean population had either attended or graduated from secondary schools.\nWhen it came to higher education, 9% of Cape Verdean men and 8% of Cape Verdean women held a bachelor\'s degree or had attended universities. The overall college education rate (i.e., college graduates and undergraduate students) in Cape Verde is about 24%, in relation to the local college age population <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.ine.cv/" rel="nofollow">[1]</a>.\nThe total expenditure on education was 5.6% of GDP (2010).\nThe mean years of schooling of adults over 25 years is 12.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Cape_Verde" title="Science and technology in Cape Verde">Science and technology in Cape Verde</a></div>\n<p>In 2011, Cape Verde devoted just 0.07% of its GDP to research and development, among the lowest rates in West Africa. The Ministry of Higher Education, Science and Culture plans to strengthen the research and academic sectors by placing emphasis on greater mobility, through exchange programmes and international co-operation agreements. As part of this strategy, Cape Verde is participating in the Ibero-American academic mobility programme that expects to mobilize 200 000 academics between 2015 and 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cape Verde counted 25 researchers in 2011, a researcher density of 51 per million inhabitants. The world average was 1,083 per million in 2013. All 25 researchers were working in the government sector in 2011 and one in three were women (36%). There was no research being conducted in either medical or agricultural sciences. Of the eight engineers involved in research and development, one was a woman. Three of the five researchers working in natural sciences were women, as were three of the six social scientists and two of the five researchers from the humanities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, the government was planning to build a \'cyber-island\' which would develop and offer services that include software development, computer maintenance and back office operations. Approved in 2013, the Praia Technology Park is a step in this direction. Financed by the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>, it is expected to be operational by 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Cape_Verde" title="Crime in Cape Verde">Crime in Cape Verde</a></div>\n<p>Theft and burglary are common in Cape Verde especially in crowds, such as market places, festivals, and celebrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-us-63">[63]</a></sup> Often the perpetrators of these crimes are gangs of street children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-us-63">[63]</a></sup> Murders are concentrated in the major population centres of Praia and Mindelo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-us-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Cape_Verde" title="Culture of Cape Verde">Culture of Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras-Musiciens.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2306" data-file-width="3218" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras-Musiciens.jpg/220px-Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras-Musiciens.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras-Musiciens.jpg/330px-Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras-Musiciens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras-Musiciens.jpg/440px-Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras-Musiciens.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras-Musiciens.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cape Verdeans are a very musical people; The <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A3_das_Caldeiras" title="Ch&#227; das Caldeiras">Ch&#227; das Caldeiras</a> group is an example.</div></div></div>\n<p>The culture of Cape Verde is characterized by a mixture of European and African elements. This is not a sum of two cultures living side by side, but a new culture resulting from an exchange that began in the 15th century.\n</p><p>The Cape Verdean case may be situated in the common context of African nations, in which elites, who questioned European racial and cultural superiority and who in some cases undertook a long armed struggle against European imperialism and national liberation, use the rule of Western codes as the main instrument of internal domination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-10"><a href="#cite_note-pc-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cape Verdean social and cultural patterns are similar to those of rural Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-11"><a href="#cite_note-pc-27">[27]</a></sup> Football games and church activities are typical sources of social interaction and entertainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-12"><a href="#cite_note-pc-27">[27]</a></sup> The traditional walk around the pra&#231;a (<a href="/wiki/Town_square" title="Town square">town square</a>) to meet friends is practiced regularly in Cape Verde towns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-13"><a href="#cite_note-pc-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Cape_Verde" title="Media of Cape Verde">Media of Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newspapers_of_Cape_Verde.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Newspapers_of_Cape_Verde.jpg/220px-Newspapers_of_Cape_Verde.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Newspapers_of_Cape_Verde.jpg/330px-Newspapers_of_Cape_Verde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Newspapers_of_Cape_Verde.jpg/440px-Newspapers_of_Cape_Verde.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newspapers_of_Cape_Verde.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Newspapers of Cape Verde including <i>Expresso das Ilhas</i>, <i>A Na&#231;&#227;o</i> and <i>J&#225;</i></div></div></div>\n<p>In towns with electricity, television is available on three channels; one state owned (<a href="/wiki/RTC_(Cape_Verde)" title="RTC (Cape Verde)">RTC</a> - TCV) and three foreign owned, RTI Cabo Verde launched by the Portuguese-based RTI in 2005, on 31 March 2007, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Record_Cabo_Verde" title="Record Cabo Verde">Record Cabo Verde</a>, its own version was launched by the Brazilian-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rede_Record" title="Rede Record">Rede Record</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-14"><a href="#cite_note-pc-27">[27]</a></sup> Cape Verde has now received <a href="/wiki/TV_CPLP" title="TV CPLP">TV CPLP</a> and some of its programs are broadcast, the network first aired in 2016. Premium channels includes the Capeverdean versions of Boom TV and Zap Cabo Verde, two channels owned by Brazil\'s Record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Other premium channels are aired in Cape Verde especially Satellite Network, they are common in hotels and villas but availability is predominantly limited, one of them is <a href="/wiki/RDP_%C3%81frica" title="RDP &#193;frica">RDP &#193;frica</a>, the African version of the Portuguese radio station <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radiodifus%C3%A3o_Portuguesa" title="Radiodifus&#227;o Portuguesa">RDP</a>.\n</p><p>As of early 2017, about 19% of the Cape Verdean population own an active cellular phone, 70% have access to the Internet, 11% own a landline telephone, and 2% of the population subscribe to local cable TV. In 2003, Cape Verde had 71,700 main line telephones with an additional 53,300 cellular phones in use throughout the country.\n</p><p>In 2004, there were seven radio stations; six independent and one state owned. The media is operated by the Capeverdean News Agency (secondarily as <a href="/wiki/Inforpress" title="Inforpress">Inforpress</a>). Nationwide radio stations include RCV, RCV+, Radio Kriola, the religious station Radio Nova.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Local radio stations include R&#225;dio Praia, the first radio station in Cape Verde, Praia FM, the first FM station in the nation, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A1dio_Barlavento" title="R&#225;dio Barlavento">R&#225;dio Barlavento</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A1dio_Clube_do_Mindelo" title="R&#225;dio Clube do Mindelo">R&#225;dio Clube do Mindelo</a> and Radio Morabeza in Mindelo.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Cape_Verde" title="Music of Cape Verde">Music of Cape Verde</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_(3).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="685" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_%283%29.jpg/220px-Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_%283%29.jpg/330px-Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_%283%29.jpg/440px-Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_(3).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora" title="Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora">Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora</a>, Cape Verdean singer</div></div></div>\n<p>The Cape Verdean people are known for their musicality, well expressed by popular manifestations such as the Carnival of Mindelo. Cape Verde music incorporates "African, Portuguese and Brazilian influences."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manuel_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-manuel-65">[65]</a></sup> Cape Verde\'s quintessential national music is the <i><a href="/wiki/Morna_(music)" title="Morna (music)">morna</a></i>, a melancholy and lyrical song form typically sung in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">Cape Verdean Creole</a>. The most popular music genre after <i><a href="/wiki/Morna_(music)" title="Morna (music)">morna</a></i> is the <i><a href="/wiki/Coladeira" title="Coladeira">coladeira</a></i>, followed by <i><a href="/wiki/Funan%C3%A1" title="Funan&#225;">funan&#225;</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batuque_(music)" title="Batuque (music)">batuque</a></i> music. <a href="/wiki/Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora" title="Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora">Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora</a> was the best-known Cape Verdean singer in the world, known as the "barefoot diva", because she liked to perform barefooted on stage. The international success of Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora has made other Cape Verdean artists, or descendants of Cape Verdeans born in Portugal, gain more space in the music market. Examples of this are singers Sara Tavares, Lura and <a href="/wiki/Mayra_Andrade" title="Mayra Andrade">Mayra Andrade</a>.\n</p><p>Another great exponent of traditional music from Cape Verde was Antonio Vicente Lopes, better known as Travadinha and <a href="/wiki/Ildo_Lobo" title="Ildo Lobo">Ildo Lobo</a>, who died in 2004. The House of Culture in the center of the city of Praia is called Ildo Lobo House of Culture, in his honor.\n</p><p>There are also well known artists born to Cape Verdean parents who excelled themselves in the international music scene. Amongst these artists are jazz pianist <a href="/wiki/Horace_Silver" title="Horace Silver">Horace Silver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_Ellington" title="Duke Ellington">Duke Ellington</a>\'s saxophonist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gonsalves" title="Paul Gonsalves">Paul Gonsalves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Te%C3%B3filo_Chantre" title="Te&#243;filo Chantre">Te&#243;filo Chantre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pena" title="Paul Pena">Paul Pena</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tavares_(group)" title="Tavares (group)">Tavares</a> brothers and singer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lura_(musician)" title="Lura (musician)">Lura</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dance">Dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Dance forms include the soft dance <i>morna</i>, the extreme sensuality of <i><a href="/wiki/Coladeira" title="Coladeira">coladeira</a></i>, the Cape Verdean version of the <a href="/wiki/Zouk" title="Zouk">zouk</a> from <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabo_love" title="Cabo love">Cabo love</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Funan%C3%A1" title="Funan&#225;">Funan&#225;</a></i> (a sensual mixed Portuguese and African dance), the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batuque_(music)" title="Batuque (music)">Batuque</a></i> dance, and the Cabo Zouk.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Praia-Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Praia-Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_%281%29.jpg/220px-Praia-Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Praia-Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_%281%29.jpg/330px-Praia-Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Praia-Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_%281%29.jpg/440px-Praia-Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Praia-Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Funda&#231;&#227;o Am&#237;lcar Cabral</i>, in Praia</div></div></div>\n<p>Cape Verdean literature is one of the richest of <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> Africa. Famous poets include Paulino Vieira, Manuel de Novas, Sergio Frusoni, Eug&#233;nio Tavares, and B. L&#233;za, and famous authors include <a href="/wiki/Baltasar_Lopes_da_Silva" title="Baltasar Lopes da Silva">Baltasar Lopes da Silva</a>, Ant&#243;nio Aur&#233;lio Gon&#231;alves, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Lopes" title="Manuel Lopes">Manuel Lopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orlanda_Amar%C3%ADlis" title="Orlanda Amar&#237;lis">Orlanda Amar&#237;lis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henrique_Teixeira_de_Sousa" title="Henrique Teixeira de Sousa">Henrique Teixeira de Sousa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arm%C3%A9nio_Vieira" title="Arm&#233;nio Vieira">Arm&#233;nio Vieira</a>, Kaoberdiano Dambar&#225;, Dr. Az&#225;gua, and <a href="/wiki/Germano_Almeida" title="Germano Almeida">Germano Almeida</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Carnival and the island of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_Cape_Verde" title="S&#227;o Vicente, Cape Verde">S&#227;o Vicente</a> is portrayed in the 2015 feature documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Tchindas" title="Tchindas">Tchindas</a></i>, nominated at the <a href="/wiki/12th_Africa_Movie_Academy_Awards" title="12th Africa Movie Academy Awards">12th Africa Movie Academy Awards</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cachupa_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Cachupa_2.jpg/220px-Cachupa_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Cachupa_2.jpg/330px-Cachupa_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Cachupa_2.jpg/440px-Cachupa_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cachupa_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cachupa, typical Cape Verdean dish</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_cuisine" title="Cape Verdean cuisine">Cape Verdean cuisine</a></div>\n<p>The Cape Verde diet is mostly based on fish and staple foods like corn and rice. Vegetables available during most of the year are potatoes, onions, tomatoes, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manioc" title="Manioc">manioc</a>, cabbage, kale, and dried beans. Fruits such as bananas and <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papayas</a> are available year-round, while others like <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocados</a> are seasonal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-15"><a href="#cite_note-pc-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A popular dish served in Cape Verde is <a href="/wiki/Cachupa" title="Cachupa">Cachupa</a>, a slow cooked stew of corn (hominy), beans, and fish or meat. A common appetizer is the <a href="/wiki/Pastel_(food)" title="Pastel (food)">pastel</a> which is a pastry shell filled with fish or meat that is then fried.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-16"><a href="#cite_note-pc-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The country\'s most successful sports team is the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_national_basketball_team" title="Cape Verde national basketball team">Cape Verde national basketball team</a>, which won the bronze medal at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship_2007" title="FIBA Africa Championship 2007">FIBA Africa Championship 2007</a>, after beating <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_basketball_team" title="Egypt national basketball team">Egypt</a> in its last game. The country\'s most well-known player is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walter_Tavares" title="Walter Tavares">Walter Tavares</a>, who plays for <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_Baloncesto" title="Real Madrid Baloncesto">Real Madrid</a> of Spain.\n</p><p>Cape Verde is famous for wave sailing (a type of windsurfing) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitesurfing" title="Kitesurfing">kiteboarding</a>. Josh Angulo, a Hawaiian and 2009 PWA Wave World Champion, has done much to promote the archipelago as a <a href="/wiki/Windsurfing" title="Windsurfing">windsurfing</a> destination. Cape Verde is now his adopted country. Mitu Monteiro, a local kitesurfer, was the 2008 <a href="/wiki/International_Kiteboarding_Association#Wave_Riding" title="International Kiteboarding Association">Kite Surfing World Champion</a> in the wave discipline.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_national_football_team" title="Cape Verde national football team">Cape Verde national football team</a>, nicknamed either the <i>Tubar&#245;es Azuis</i> (Blue Sharks) or <i>Crioulos</i> (Creoles), is the national team of Cape Verde and is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Football_Federation" title="Cape Verdean Football Federation">Cape Verdean Football Federation</a>. The team has played at two <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a>, in <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations">2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2015 Africa Cup of Nations">2015</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The country has competed at every <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> since 1996.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cape_Verde" title="Transport in Cape Verde">Transport in Cape Verde</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">Ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Ports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CaisPortoNovo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/CaisPortoNovo.JPG/220px-CaisPortoNovo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/CaisPortoNovo.JPG/330px-CaisPortoNovo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/CaisPortoNovo.JPG/440px-CaisPortoNovo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CaisPortoNovo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>New port in Santo Ant&#227;o</div></div></div>\n<p>There are four international ports: Mindelo, S&#227;o Vicente; Praia, Santiago; Palmeira, Sal; and Sal Rei, Boa Vista. Mindelo on S&#227;o Vicente is the main port for cruise liners and the terminus for the ferry service to Santo Ant&#227;o. Praia on Santiago is a main hub for local ferry services to other islands. Palmeira on Sal supplies fuel for the main airport on the island, Am&#237;lcar Cabral International Airport, and is important for the hotel construction taking place on the island. Porto Novo on Santo Ant&#227;o is the only source for imports and exports of produce from the island as well as passenger traffic since the closure of the airstrip at Ponta do Sol.\nThere are smaller harbors, essentially single jetties at Tarrafal on S&#227;o Nicolau, Sal Rei on Boa Vista, Vila do Maio (Porto Ingl&#234;s) on Maio, S&#227;o Filipe on Fogo and Furna on Brava. These act as terminals for the inter-island ferry services, which carry both freight and passengers. The pier at Santa Maria on Sal used by both fishing and dive boats has been rehabilitated.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroporto-Internacional-Aristides-Pereira-Terminal-2012.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3436" data-file-width="4570" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Aeroporto-Internacional-Aristides-Pereira-Terminal-2012.JPG/220px-Aeroporto-Internacional-Aristides-Pereira-Terminal-2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Aeroporto-Internacional-Aristides-Pereira-Terminal-2012.JPG/330px-Aeroporto-Internacional-Aristides-Pereira-Terminal-2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Aeroporto-Internacional-Aristides-Pereira-Terminal-2012.JPG/440px-Aeroporto-Internacional-Aristides-Pereira-Terminal-2012.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroporto-Internacional-Aristides-Pereira-Terminal-2012.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Aristides_Pereira_International_Airport" title="Aristides Pereira International Airport">Aristides Pereira International Airport</a> in Boa Vista island</div></div></div>\n<p>There were seven operational airports as of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>&#160;&#8212; 4 international and 3 domestic. Two others were non-operational, one on Brava and the other on Santo Ant&#227;o, closed for safety reasons.\n</p><p>Due to its geographical location, Cape Verde is often flown over by transatlantic airliners. It is part of the conventional air-traffic route from <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> to <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, which goes from southern <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> and Cape Verde to northern <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_airports">International airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: International airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral_International_Airport" title="Am&#237;lcar Cabral International Airport">Am&#237;lcar Cabral International Airport</a>, Sal Island</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_International_Airport" title="Nelson Mandela International Airport">Nelson Mandela International Airport</a>, Santiago Island</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aristides_Pereira_International_Airport" title="Aristides Pereira International Airport">Aristides Pereira International Airport</a>, Boa Vista Island</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ces%C3%A1ria_%C3%89vora_Airport" title="Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora Airport">Ces&#225;ria &#201;vora Airport</a>, S&#227;o Vicente Island</li>\n<li>Jo&#227;o dos Santos Airport, CPV</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals"
